Testing\n\n**DO:**\n- Test graceful shutdown explicitly\n- Simulate signals in tests\n- Verify cleanup runs\n- Test timeout conditions\n- Verify no data loss\n\n**DON'T:**\n- Skip shutdown testing\n- Only test happy path\n- Assume cleanup works\n- Test with real signals in CI\n\n---\n\n## Part 6: Common Pitfalls and Solutions\n\n### Pitfall 1: Lost Signals\n```go\n// WRONG - unbuffered channel loses signals\nsig := make(chan os.Signal)\nsignal.Notify(sig, syscall.SIGTERM)\n\n// CORRECT - buffered channel preserves signals\nsig := make(chan os.Signal, 1)\nsignal.Notify(sig, syscall.SIGTERM)\n```\n\n### Pitfall 2: Infinite Waiting\n```go\n// WRONG - can block forever\nserver.Shutdown(context.Background())\n\n// CORRECT - bounded wait\nctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(context.Background(), 30*time.Second)\ndefer cancel()\nserver.Shutdown(ctx)\n```\n\n### Pitfall 3: Goroutine Leaks\n```go\n// WRONG - goroutine never exits\ngo func() {\n    for {\n        doWork()\n    }\n}()\n\n// CORRECT - responds to context\ngo func() {\n    for {\n        select {\n        case <-ctx.Done():\n            return\n        case <-workChan:\n            doWork()\n        }\n    }\n}()\n```\n\n### Pitfall 4: Race Conditions\n```go\n// WRONG - concurrent shutdown calls\ns.shutdown()\ns.shutdown()  // Called again\n\n// CORRECT - synchronized with sync.Once\ns.shutdownOnce.Do(func() {\n    s.shutdown()\n})\n```\n\n### Pitfall 5: Lost Context\n```go\n// WRONG - inner function ignores context\nfunc handleRequest(ctx context.Context) {\n    time.Sleep(10*time.Second)  // Can't be interrupted\n}\n\n// CORRECT - respects context\nfunc handleRequest(ctx context.Context) {\n    select {\n    case <-ctx.Done():\n        return\n    case <-time.After(10*time.Second):\n        // Process result\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Part 7: File Reference Guide\n\n### Kubernetes Files\n\n| File | Purpose | Key Symbols |\n|------|---------|---|\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal.go` | Core signal handler | `SetupSignalContext()` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal_posix.go` | POSIX signals | `shutdownSignals` |\n| `pkg/util/interrupt/interrupt.go` | Advanced interrupt handler | `Handler`, `Run()` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/sample-controller/pkg/signals/signal.go` | Template | Reference implementation |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/examples/leader-election/main.go` | Leader election pattern | Complete example |\n\n### Prometheus Files\n\n| File | Purpose | Key Symbols |\n|------|---------|---|\n| `cmd/prometheus/main.go` | Signal handling + orchestration | `run.Group`, signal handlers (lines 1151+) |\n| `cmd/prometheus/main.go` | Feature flags | `DrainOnShutdown` (line 582) |\n| `cmd/prometheus/main.go` | Memory snapshot | `EnableMemorySnapshotOnShutdown` (line 234) |\n\n### Grafana Files\n\n| File | Purpose | Key Symbols |\n|------|---------|---|\n| `pkg/cmd/grafana-server/commands/cli.go` | Signal listener | `listenToSystemSignals()` (lines 148-170) |\n| `pkg/server/server.go` | Server lifecycle | `Shutdown()`, `notifySystemd()` |\n| `pkg/api/http_server.go` | HTTP shutdown | `Start()`, graceful shutdown (lines 490+) |\n\n---\n\n## Part 8: Conclusion\n\nAll three projects implement graceful shutdown successfully using:\n\n1. **Core Signal Handling**: `os/signal.Notify()` with buffered channels\n2. **Signals**: SIGTERM and SIGINT for shutdown, SIGHUP for reload\n3. **Coordination**: Context, run.Group, or sync.Once depending on complexity\n4. **Cleanup**: Ordered shutdown of components, draining before stopping\n5. **Timeouts**: Explicit bounds to prevent hanging processes\n\n**Choose your pattern based on needs:**\n\n| Requirement | Best Pattern |\n|------------|---|\n| Simple service with few components | **Kubernetes (context)** |\n| Complex system with many services | **Prometheus (run.Group)** |\n| HTTP service needing strict timeout | **Grafana (explicit timeout)** |\n| Learning/reference implementation | **Kubernetes sample-controller** |\n\nAll three patterns are production-proven and handle the critical requirement: **graceful shutdown without losing data**."

Container/systemd shutdown | \u2713 | \u2713 | \u2713 |\n| SIGINT | Terminal interrupt (Ctrl+C) | \u2713 | \u2713 | \u2713 |\n| SIGHUP | Reload config/logs | \u2717 | \u2713 | \u2713 |\n\n### Signal Registration\n\n```go\n// All three use buffered channels\nch := make(chan os.Signal, 1)  // or 2 for Kubernetes\nsignal.Notify(ch, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)\n```\n\n### On First Signal\n- **Kubernetes**: Cancel context\n- **Prometheus**: Log and initiate cleanup\n- **Grafana**: Apply timeout, start shutdown\n\n### On Second Signal\n- **Kubernetes**: Force exit with code 1\n- **Prometheus**: Natural exit from run.Group\n- **Grafana**: Already exited after first signal\n\n---\n\n## Key Learnings\n\n### 1. Use Buffered Channels\n```go\n// Buffer size 1-2 to prevent losing signals\nch := make(chan os.Signal, 1)\nsignal.Notify(ch, syscall.SIGTERM)\n```\n\n### 2. Always Use Timeouts\n```go\n// Prevent infinite waiting during shutdown\nctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(ctx, 30*time.Second)\ndefer cancel()\nserver.Shutdown(ctx)\n```\n\n### 3. Ensure Single Execution\n```go\n// Use sync.Once for shutdown code\ns.shutdownOnce.Do(func() {\n    // Shutdown code runs exactly once\n})\n```\n\n### 4. Explicit Cleanup Order\n```go\n// Stop accepting connections \u2192 drain requests \u2192 stop workers \u2192 flush data\ng.Add(stopConnections, nil)\ng.Add(drainRequests, nil)\ng.Add(stopWorkers, nil)\ng.Add(flushData, nil)\n```\n\n### 5. Pass Context Through Call Chain\n```go\nfunc handleRequest(ctx context.Context) {\n    select {\n    case <-ctx.Done():\n        return  // Stop immediately when context cancelled\n    case <-work:\n        doWork()\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## File Structure\n\nRepository files are located at:\n\n### Kubernetes\n- Base: `/tmp/kubernetes/`\n- Signal handler: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal.go`\n- Advanced handler: `pkg/util/interrupt/interrupt.go`\n- Example: `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/examples/leader-election/main.go`\n\n### Prometheus\n- Base: `/tmp/prometheus/`\n- Main: `cmd/prometheus/main.go`\n\n### Grafana\n- Base: `/tmp/grafana/`\n- Signal handler: `pkg/cmd/grafana-server/commands/cli.go`\n- Server: `pkg/server/server.go`\n- HTTP server: `pkg/api/http_server.go`\n\n---\n\n## Testing Checklist\n\nWhen implementing graceful shutdown:\n\n- [ ] Register signal handler early\n- [ ] Use buffered channel (size \u2265 1)\n- [ ] Handle SIGTERM and SIGINT\n- [ ] Implement timeout (30-60 seconds)\n- [ ] Ensure cleanup runs exactly once\n- [ ] Stop connections before workers\n- [ ] Log shutdown events\n- [ ] Test with actual signals\n- [ ] Test timeout scenario\n- [ ] Verify no data loss\n\n---\n\n## Common Mistakes to Avoid\n\n1. **Unbuffered signal channels** - Signals can be lost\n2. **No timeout** - Process can hang indefinitely\n3. **Multiple shutdown calls** - Can corrupt state\n4. **Wrong cleanup order** - Workers writing to closed databases\n5. **Not respecting context** - Goroutines don't see cancellation\n6. **Silent errors** - Hard to debug shutdown failures\n\n---\n\n## Related Concepts\n\n### Docker/Container Context\n- Container sends SIGTERM on stop\n- Default timeout: 30 seconds (configurable with StopTimeout)\n- Then sends SIGKILL if process hasn't exited\n\n### Systemd Context\n- Sends SIGTERM on stop\n- Respects `TimeoutStopSec=` in service file\n- Can use `Type=notify` with `sd_notify()` for readiness\n- Grafana implements `notifySystemd(\"READY=1\")`\n\n### Kubernetes Context\n- Graceful termination period: 30 seconds (configurable)\n- POD lifecycle hooks available (PreStop)\n- Health check endpoints should return not-ready during shutdown\n\n---\n\n## References\n\n### Original Repositories\n- Kubernetes: https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes\n- Prometheus: https://github.com/prometheus/prometheus\n- Grafana: https://github.com/grafana/grafana\n\n### Go Standard Library\n- `os/signal` - Signal handling\n- `context` - Context-based cancellation\n- `sync` - Synchronization primitives\n- `net/http` - HTTP server graceful shutdown\n\n### External Dependencies\n- `github.com/oklog/run` - Always Use Timeout\n```go\nctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(ctx, 30*time.Second)\ndefer cancel()\nserver.Shutdown(ctx)  // Won't hang forever\n```\n\n### 3. Ensure Single Execution\n```go\ns.shutdownOnce.Do(func() {\n    // This code runs exactly once\n})\n```\n\n### 4. Log Everything\n```go\nlogger.Info(\"Shutdown started\", \"reason\", reason)\nlogger.Warn(\"Timed out waiting for shutdown\")\nlogger.Info(\"Shutdown complete\")\n```\n\n### 5. Pass Context Through Call Stack\n```go\nfunc handler(ctx context.Context) {\n    select {\n    case <-ctx.Done():\n        return  // Responds to cancellation\n    case <-workChan:\n        doWork()\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Recommended Reading Order\n\n### For Quick Implementation (30 minutes)\n1. Use Buffered Channels\n```go\nch := make(chan os.Signal, 1)  // Don't use unbuffered\nsignal.Notify(ch, syscall.SIGTERM, os.Interrupt)\n```\n\n### 2. Always Use Timeout\n```go\nctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(ctx, 30*time.Second)\ndefer cancel()\nserver.Shutdown(ctx)  // Won't hang forever\n```\n\n### 3. Ensure Single Execution\n```go\ns.shutdownOnce.Do(func() {\n    // This code runs exactly once\n})\n```\n\n### 4. Log Everything\n```go\nlogger.Info(\"Shutdown started\", \"reason\", reason)\nlogger.Warn(\"Timed out waiting for shutdown\")\nlogger.Info(\"Shutdown complete\")\n```\n\n### 5. Pass Context Through Call Stack\n```go\nfunc handler(ctx context.Context) {\n    select {\n    case <-ctx.Done():\n        return  // Responds to cancellation\n    case <-workChan:\n        doWork()\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Recommended Reading Order\n\n### For Quick Implementation (30 minutes)\n1. (size \u2265 1)\n\nPITFALL 2: Infinite Wait\nProblem: Cleanup blocks forever, process never exits\nSolution: Always use context.WithTimeout for external operations\n\nPITFALL 3: Duplicate Shutdown\nProblem: Shutdown runs multiple times, corrupts state\nSolution: Use sync.Once for all shutdown code\n\nPITFALL 4: Lost Cleanup\nProblem: Some goroutines don't see cancellation\nSolution: Explicit cleanup functions per component\n  - Clear dependency ordering\n  - All cleanups guaranteed to run\n  - Fine-grained control\n  - 20+ goroutines coordinated seamlessly\n\nPATTERN 3: EXPLICIT TIMEOUT (Grafana)\n------------------------------------\nRepository: github.com/grafana/grafana\nKey Files: pkg/cmd/grafana-server/commands/cli.go\n           pkg/server/server.go\n           pkg/api/http_server.go\n\nPattern:\n  <-signalChan\n  ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(ctx, 30*time.Second)\n  defer cancel()\n  server.Shutdown(ctx)  // Bounded graceful shutdown\n\nBest For: HTTP services needing bounded shutdown\nComplexity: Medium\nDependencies: Standard library + sync/errgroup\nSignals: SIGTERM, SIGINT (SIGHUP for log reload)\n\nKey Features:\n  - Explicit 30-second timeout prevents hanging\n  - sync.Once ensures single execution\n  - Separate signal channels for different purposes\n  - Systemd integration for container orchestration\n  - HTTP server graceful shutdown with in-flight request handling\n\n================================================================================\n                         SIGNAL HANDLING SUMMARY\n================================================================================\n\nAll three projects use: os/signal.Notify() with buffered channels\n\nSignals Handled:\n  SIGTERM    - Container/systemd shutdown signal (primary)\n  SIGINT     - Terminal interrupt (Ctrl+C)\n  SIGHUP     - Config/log reload (Prometheus & Grafana)\n\nBuffer Sizes:\n  Kubernetes: 2 (for 1st + 2nd signal)\n  Prometheus: 1\n  Grafana:    1 per signal type\n\nRegistration Pattern:\n  ch := make(chan os.Signal, 1)\n  signal.Notify(ch, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)\n\n================================================================================\n                        KEY IMPLEMENTATION POINTS\n================================================================================\n\n1. USE BUFFERED CHANNELS\n   \u2713 ch := make(chan os.Signal, 1)\n   \u2717 ch := make(chan os.Signal)\n\n2. ALWAYS USE TIMEOUT\n   \u2713 ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(ctx, 30*time.Second)\n   \u2717 server.Shutdown(context.Background())\n\n3. ENSURE SINGLE EXECUTION\n   \u2713 s.shutdownOnce.Do(func() { cleanup() })\n   \u2717 Multiple shutdown() calls possible\n\n4. EXPLICIT CLEANUP ORDER\n   Kubernetes: Implicit through context propagation\n   Prometheus: Explicit in run.Group order\n   Grafana: Layered (HTTP \u2192 Services \u2192 Cleanup)\n\n5. PASS CONTEXT THROUGH CALL STACK\n   \u2713 func handler(ctx context.Context) { <-ctx.Done() }\n   \u2717 func handler() { time.Sleep(...) } // Can't interrupt\n\n6. LOG SHUTDOWN EVENTS\n   - Shutdown started (with reason)\n   - Timeout warnings\n   - Shutdown completion\n   - Error conditions\n\n================================================================================\n                         GRACEFUL SHUTDOWN FLOW\n================================================================================\n\nAll three projects follow this general flow:\n\nOS Signal (SIGTERM)\n    \u2193\nSignal Handler (os/signal.Notify)\n    \u2193\nContext Cancellation or Channel Communication\n    \u2193\nAll Components Informed\n    \u2193\nStop Accepting New Requests\n    \u2193\nDrain In-Flight Requests (with timeout)\n    \u2193\nStop Background Goroutines\n    \u2193\nFlush Data to Storage\n    \u2193\nClose Resources\n    \u2193\nProcess Exits (0 for success, 1 for timeout)\n\nTimeout typically: 30-60 setupSignalHandler() context.Context {\n    ch := make(chan os.Signal, 1)\n    signal.Notify(ch, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)\n    ctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())\n    go func() {\n        <-ch\n        cancel()       // First signal\n        <-ch\n        os.Exit(1)     // Second signal\n    }()\n    return ctx\n}\n\nWITH TIMEOUT (Copy-Paste PITFALLS\n================================================================================\n\nPITFALL 1: Lost Signals\nProblem: Signal arrives before handler registered\nSolution: Use buffered channel (size \u2265 1)\n\nPITFALL 2: Infinite Wait\nProblem: Cleanup blocks forever, process never exits\nSolution: Always use context.WithTimeout for external operations\n\nPITFALL 3: Duplicate Shutdown\nProblem: Shutdown runs multiple times, corrupts state\nSolution: Use sync.Once for all shutdown code\n\nPITFALL 4: Lost Cleanup\nProblem: Some goroutines don't see cancellation\nSolution: Container orchestration platform\n2. **Prometheus** - Time series database and monitoring system  \n3. **Grafana** - Metrics visualization and alerting platform\n\nAll code examples are extracted from official GitHub repositories and represent current best practices.\n\n---\n\n## Part 1: Core Concepts\n\n### What is Graceful Shutdown?\n\nGraceful shutdown is the process of safely terminating a running application while:\n- Completing in-flight requests\n- Persisting pending data\n- Draining queues\n- Cleaning up resources\n- Notifying dependent systems\n\n### Why It Matters\n\n- **Data Integrity**: Prevents data loss during container restarts\n- **User Experience**: Requests complete rather than timeout\n- **System Health**: Proper cleanup prevents resource leaks\n- **Operational Safety**: Works seamlessly with container orchestration\n\n### Signal-Based Shutdown Flow\n\n```\nOS Signal (SIGTERM) \n    \u2193\nSignal Handler (os/signal.Notify)\n    \u2193\nContext Cancellation or Channel Communication\n    \u2193\nAll Components Informed\n    \u2193\nIn-Flight Requests Drained\n    \u2193\nBackground Services Stopped\n    \u2193\nResources Cleaned Up\n    \u2193\nProcess Exits (0 for success, 1 for timeout/error)\n```\n\n---\n\n## Part 2: Project Analysis\n\n### KUBERNETES: Context-Based Cancellation\n\n**Repository**: github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes  \n**Pattern**: Propagate context.Context through all components\n\n#### Core Files\n\n1. **staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal.go**\n   - Platform-specific signal definitions\n   - Handles: `os.Interrupt` (SIGINT), `syscall.SIGTERM`\n\n3. **pkg/util/interrupt/interrupt.go**\n   - Advanced handler with cleanup functions\n   - Guarantees cleanup executes exactly once\n   - Supports multiple signal types\n\n#### Key Characteristics\n\n| Aspect | Implementation |\n|--------|---|\n| **Signal Handling** | `signal.Notify(ch, shutdownSignals...)` |\n| **Primary Signals** | SIGINT, SIGTERM |\n| **Coordination** | `context.Context` propagation |\n| **Cleanup Pattern** | Context cancellation |\n| **Timeout** | Implicit (per-component) |\n| **Double Signal** | `os.Exit(1)` on 2nd signal |\n| **Dependencies** | Standard library only |\n\n#### Code Pattern\n\n```go\nfunc SetupSignalContext() context.Context {\n    shutdownHandler := make(chan os.Signal, 2)\n    signal.Notify(shutdownHandler, shutdownSignals...)\n    \n    ctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())\n    go func() {\n        <-shutdownHandler           // 1st signal\n        cancel()\n        <-shutdownHandler           // 2nd signal",

SIGTERM (container shutdown). The signal handler is protected by `onlyOneSignalHandler` which panics if called twice, ensuring single execution.\\n\\nThe companion file `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal_posix.go` defines `shutdownSignals` as `{os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM}` for non-Windows systems. The shutdown method delegates to `managerAdapter.Shutdown()` for background services and waits on context completion (lines 162-168), logging timeouts if they occur. HTTP graceful shutdown at `pkg/api/http_server.go` (lines 490-497) waits for context cancellation then calls `httpSrv.Shutdown()` with a fresh background context, using `http.ErrServerClosed` detection. The implementation also provides systemd integration through `notifySystemd(state string)` which sends socket notifications to systemd for proper service ordering.\\n\\nAll three patterns handle the core shutdown requirements: signal handler registration (buffered channels of size 1-2), shutdown timeouts (implicit via context in Kubernetes, per-component in Prometheus, explicit 30 seconds in Grafana), and cleanup ordering (context propagation in Kubernetes, reverse-order interrupt functions in Prometheus, layered shutdown in Grafana). The choice between patterns reflects architectural needs: Kubernetes favors simplicity through context propagation, Prometheus requires explicit component ordering, and Grafana emphasizes timeout guarantees for HTTP services. === GRACEFUL SHUTDOWN PATTERNS ACROSS KUBERNETES, PROMETHEUS, AND GRAFANA ===

PROJECT SUMMARIES:

1. KUBERNETES/KUBERNETES
   Repository: github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes
   
   Key Signal Handling Files:
   - staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal.go
   - staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal_posix.go
   - staging/src/k8s.io/sample-controller/pkg/signals/signal.go
   - staging/src/k8s.io/sample-controller/pkg/signals/signal_posix.go
   - pkg/util/interrupt/interrupt.go
   
   Key Patterns:
   - Signal Handler Registration: signal.Notify() with buffered channels (size 2)
   - Signals Handled: os.Interrupt (SIGINT) and syscall.SIGTERM
   - Context-based Cancellation: SetupSignalContext() returns context.Context
   - Graceful Degradation: 1st signal cancels context, 2nd signal exits immediately
   
   Client Example: staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/examples/leader-election/main.go
   - Uses signal.Notify() with context.WithCancel()
   - Demonstrates cleanup before shutdown
   - Leader election pattern with graceful step-down

2. PROMETHEUS/PROMETHEUS
   Repository: github.com/prometheus/prometheus
   
   Key Signal Handling File:
   - cmd/prometheus/main.go
   
   Key Patterns:
   - Signal Handler: signal.Notify(term, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)
   - Goroutine Management: Uses oklog/run.Group for coordinated shutdown
   - Log Output: "Received an OS signal, exiting gracefully..."
   - Queue Draining: Notifier.DrainOnShutdown flag (default true)
   - Signal Coordination:
     * First signal: Logs graceful shutdown message
     * Multiple shutdown triggers: OS signal, web service request, internal cancellation
   - Goroutine Orchestration: Each g.Add() call has execution and cleanup functions
   - Cleanup Order: Proper dependency ordering (scrape manager stops before TSDB close)
   
   Features:
   - Memory snapshot on shutdown capability
   - Flush deadline for remote storage writes
   - Notification queue draining before shutdown

3. GRAFANA/GRAFANA
   Repository: github.com/grafana/grafana
   
   Key Signal Handling Files:
   - pkg/cmd/grafana-server/commands/cli.go (listenToSystemSignals function)
   - pkg/server/server.go (Shutdown method)
   - pkg/api/http_server.go (graceful HTTP shutdown)
   
   Key Patterns:
   - Signal Channels: 
     * signalChan for SIGTERM/SIGINT (os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)
     * sighupChan for SIGHUP (log reload without server stop)
   - Shutdown Timeout: context.WithTimeout(ctx, 30*time.Second)
   - Shutdown Coordination:
     * Signal handler calls s.Shutdown(ctx, reason)
     * Shutdown uses sync.Once to ensure single execution
   
   Server Shutdown Implementation:
   - Graceful HTTP shutdown using http.Server.Shutdown(ctx)
   - Waits for active connections to complete
   - Handles context timeout with appropriate logging
   - ErrorGroup (sync/errgroup) for concurrent listener management
   - Detects ErrServerClosed for clean shutdown confirmation
   
   Systemd Integration:
   - notifySystemd("READY=1") after server initialization
   - NOTIFY_SOCKET environment variable detection
   - Unix domain socket communication with systemd

=== COMMON PATTERNS ACROSS ALL THREE ===

1. Signal Registration Pattern:
   - All use signal.Notify() with buffered channels
   - Buffer size matches expected signals (typically 1-2)
   
2. Signals Handled:
   - SIGTERM (syscall.SIGTERM) - Primary graceful shutdown signal
   - SIGINT (os.Interrupt) - Terminal interrupt, graceful shutdown
   - SIGHUP (syscall.SIGHUP, Grafana only) - Reload signal
   
3. Context-Based Flow Control:
   - Kubernetes: context.Context from signal handler
   - Prometheus: Channel-based coordination with run.Group
   - Grafana: context.WithTimeout for bounded shutdown
   
4. Multi-Signal Handling:
   - Kubernetes: 2nd signal exits immediately (os.Exit(1))
   - Prometheus: Web service can also trigger shutdown
   - Grafana: SIGHUP handled separately from SIGTERM/SIGINT
   
5. Graceful Shutdown Cleanup Order:
   - Close inbound connections/listeners
   - Wait for in-flight requests
   - Drain queues/buffers
   - Stop background goroutines
   - Close database/storage
   - Cleanup resources
   
6. Timeout Management:
   - Grafana explicitly uses 30-second timeout
   - Prometheus: Depends on each component's shutdown implementation
   - Kubernetes: Context-based with implicit timeout handling

# Graceful Shutdown Patterns - Code Examples

## 1. KUBERNETES - Basic Signal Handler Pattern

### File: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal.go`
```go
// SetupSignalContext returns a context that is cancelled on SIGTERM or SIGINT
func SetupSignalContext() context.Context {
    close(onlyOneSignalHandler) // panic if called twice
    
    shutdownHandler = make(chan os.Signal, 2)
    ctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())
    
    signal.Notify(shutdownHandler, shutdownSignals...)
    go func() {
        <-shutdownHandler           // First signal cancels context
        cancel()
        <-shutdownHandler           // Second signal exits immediately
        os.Exit(1)
    }()
    
    return ctx
}
```

### File: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal_posix.go`
```go
var shutdownSignals = []os.Signal{os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM}
```

### Key Principles:
- Single signal handler ensures no duplicate registrations
- 2-capacity channel prevents losing signals
- First signal triggers graceful shutdown
- Second signal force-exits with code 1
- Returns context for dependency tracking

---

## 2. KUBERNETES - Advanced Interrupt Handler

### File: `pkg/util/interrupt/interrupt.go`
```go
var terminationSignals = []os.Signal{
    syscall.SIGHUP, syscall.SIGINT, syscall.SIGTERM, syscall.SIGQUIT
}

type Handler struct {
    notify []func()              // Cleanup functions
    final  func(os.Signal)       // Final handler (default: os.Exit(1))
    once   sync.Once             // Ensure single execution
}

// Run wraps the critical section with cleanup guarantee
func (h *Handler) Run(fn func() error) error {
    ch := make(chan os.Signal, 1)
    signal.Notify(ch, terminationSignals...)
    defer func() {
        signal.Stop(ch)
        close(ch)
    }()
    
    go func() {
        sig, ok := <-ch
        if !ok {
            return
        }
        h.Signal(sig)  // Executes all notify functions
    }()
    
    defer h.Close()    // Ensures cleanup on normal exit
    return fn()        // Run protected code
}
```

### Key Principles:
- sync.Once ensures cleanup runs exactly once
- Multiple notification functions run in order
- Cleanup guaranteed even on panic
- Signal channel cleaned up properly

---

## 3. KUBERNETES - Leader Election Example

### File: `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/examples/leader-election/main.go`
```go
func main() {
    // Create cancellable context for coordinated shutdown
    ctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())
    defer cancel()
    
    // Signal handler with early exit capability
    ch := make(chan os.Signal, 1)
    signal.Notify(ch, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)
    go func() {
        <-ch
        klog.Info("Received termination, signaling shutdown")
        cancel()  // Triggers leader election cleanup
    }()
    
    // Leader election automatically stops when context is done
    leaderelection.RunOrDie(ctx, leaderelection.LeaderElectionConfig{
        Lock: lock,
        ReleaseOnCancel: true,
        Callbacks: leaderelection.LeaderCallbacks{
            OnStartedLeading: func(ctx context.Context) {
                // Cleanup happens automatically when ctx is cancelled
                run(ctx)
            },
            OnStoppedLeading: func() {
                // Perform cleanup operations here
                os.Exit(0)
            },
        },
    })
}
```

### Key Principles:
- Context cancellation coordinates all components
- Leader election respects context deadline
- Cleanup callback runs on transition out of leadership
- No manual cleanup needed if using context properly

---

## 4. PROMETHEUS - Multi-Signal Coordination

### File: `cmd/prometheus/main.go` (lines 1150-1176)
```go
var g run.Group

// Signal handler goroutine
{
    term := make(chan os.Signal, 1)
    signal.Notify(term, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)
    cancel := make(chan struct{})
    
    g.Add(
        // Execution function
        func() error {
            select {
            case sig := <-term:
                logger.Warn("Received an OS signal, exiting gracefully...", 
                    "signal", sig.String())
                reloadReady.Close()
            case <-webHandler.Quit():
                logger.Warn("Received termination request via web service, exiting gracefully...")
            case <-cancel:
                reloadReady.Close()
            }
            return nil
        },
        // Cleanup function
        func(error) {
            close(cancel)
            webHandler.SetReady(web.Stopping)
            notifs.AddNotification(notifications.ShuttingDown)
        },
    )
}

// Scrape manager with ordered shutdown
{
    g.Add(
        // Execution
        func() error {
            err := scrapeManager.Run(discoveryManagerScrape.SyncCh())
            logger.Info("Scrape manager stopped")
            return err
        },
        // Cleanup - must happen before TSDB close
        func(error) {
            logger.Info("Stopping scrape manager...")
            scrapeManager.Stop()
        },
    )
}

// Run all goroutines until one returns
g.Run()
```

### Key Principles:
- `oklog/run.Group` manages goroutine lifecycle
- Each g.Add() has execution and cleanup functions
- All cleanup functions called when any returns
- Multiple signal sources (OS signal, web API, internal)
- Cleanup order matters (scrape before TSDB)
- Context-less but explicit cleanup

---

## 5. GRAFANA - Signal Handling with Timeout

### File: `pkg/cmd/grafana-server/commands/cli.go` (lines 148-170)
```go
func listenToSystemSignals(ctx context.Context, s gserver) {
    signalChan := make(chan os.Signal, 1)
    sighupChan := make(chan os.Signal, 1)
    
    // Separate handlers for different signals
    signal.Notify(sighupChan, syscall.SIGHUP)           // Reload logs
    signal.Notify(signalChan, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)
    
    for {
        select {
        case <-sighupChan:
            if err := log.Reload(); err != nil {
                fmt.Fprintf(os.Stderr, "Failed to reload loggers: %s\n", err)
            }
        case sig := <-signalChan:
            // Bounded shutdown timeout
            ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(ctx, 30*time.Second)
            defer cancel()
            
            if err := s.Shutdown(ctx, fmt.Sprintf("System signal: %s", sig)); err != nil {
                fmt.Fprintf(os.Stderr, "Timed out waiting for server to shut down\n")
            }
            return  // Exit signal handler
        }
    }
}
```

### File: `pkg/server/server.go` (lines 155-172)
```go
func (s *Server) Shutdown(ctx context.Context, reason string) error {
    var err error
    s.shutdownOnce.Do(func() {
        s.log.Info("Shutdown started", "reason", reason)
        
        // Call all service shutdown logic
        if shutdownErr := s.managerAdapter.Shutdown(ctx, "shutdown"); shutdownErr != nil {
            s.log.Error("Failed to shutdown background services", "error", shutdownErr)
        }
        
        // Wait for context or timeout
        select {
        case <-ctx.Done():
            s.log.Warn("Timed out while waiting for server to shut down")
            err = fmt.Errorf("timeout waiting for shutdown")
        default:
            s.log.Debug("Finished waiting for server to shut down")
        }
    })
    
    return err
}
```

### File: `pkg/api/http_server.go` (lines 490-497)
```go
go func() {
    defer wg.Done()
    
    <-ctx.Done()
    // Use background context for HTTP shutdown - don't inherit timeout
    if err := hs.httpSrv.Shutdown(context.Background()); err != nil {
        hs.log.Error("Failed to shutdown server", "error", err)
    }
}()

// Concurrent listener serving
errg, _ := errgroup.WithContext(ctx)
for _, listener := range listeners {
    errg.Go(func() error {
        err := hs.httpSrv.Serve(listener)
        if errors.Is(err, http.ErrServerClosed) {
            hs.log.Debug("server was shutdown gracefully")
            return nil
        }
        return err
    })
}
```

### Key Principles:
- Explicit 30-second shutdown timeout
- sync.Once ensures single shutdown execution
- Separate signal channels for different signals (SIGHUP vs SIGTERM)
- HTTP shutdown uses fresh background context (no timeout inheritance)
- ErrorGroup manages concurrent listeners
- Expects http.ErrServerClosed for clean shutdown detection

---

## 6. GRAFANA - Systemd Integration

### File: `pkg/server/server.go` (lines 198-226)
```go
func (s *Server) notifySystemd(state string) {
    notifySocket := os.Getenv("NOTIFY_SOCKET")
    if notifySocket == "" {
        return
    }
    
    socketAddr := &net.UnixAddr{
        Name: notifySocket,
        Net:  "unixgram",
    }
    conn, err := net.DialUnix(socketAddr.Net, nil, socketAddr)
    if err != nil {
        s.log.Warn("Failed to connect to systemd", "err", err)
        return
    }
    defer func() {
        if err := conn.Close(); err != nil {
            s.log.Warn("Failed to close connection", "err", err)
        }
    }()
    
    _, err = conn.Write([]byte(state))
    if err != nil {
        s.log.Warn("Failed to write notification to systemd", "err", err)
    }
}

// In Run():
s.notifySystemd("READY=1")
```

### Key Principles:
- Systemd notification via Unix socket
- Communicates readiness to systemd
- Optional feature (gracefully degrades if socket unavailable)
- Enables systemd socket activation and service ordering

---

## Summary Table

| Aspect | Kubernetes | Prometheus | Grafana |
|--------|-----------|-----------|---------|
| **Signal Handling** | signal.Notify with context | signal.Notify with channels | signal.Notify with separate channels |
| **Signals** | SIGINT, SIGTERM | SIGINT, SIGTERM | SIGINT, SIGTERM, SIGHUP |
| **Goroutine Management** | Context-based | oklog/run.Group | sync/errgroup + context |
| **Shutdown Timeout** | Implicit | Per-component | 30 seconds explicit |
| **Double Signal** | os.Exit(1) | No special handling | N/A |
| **Cleanup Pattern** | Context cancellation | Cleanup functions | sync.Once + context |
| **Systemd Integration** | No | No | Yes (optional) |

## Comparison: Signal Configuration Summary

### Signal Registration Patterns

| Project | Primary Signal Channel | Buffer Size | Signals | Approach |
|---------|----------------------|-------------|---------|----------|
| Kubernetes (apiserver) | `shutdownHandler` | 2 | SIGINT, SIGTERM | Context cancellation |
| Kubernetes (sample) | `c` | 2 | SIGINT, SIGTERM | Context cancellation |
| Kubernetes (interrupt) | `ch` | 1 | SIGHUP, SIGINT, SIGTERM, SIGQUIT | Callback functions |
| Kubernetes (client-go) | `ch` | 1 | SIGINT, SIGTERM | Context cancellation |
| Prometheus | `term` | 1 | SIGINT, SIGTERM | run.Group coordination |
| Prometheus | `hup` | 1 | SIGHUP | Config reload |
| Grafana | `signalChan` | 1 | SIGINT, SIGTERM | Timeout + sync.Once |
| Grafana | `sighupChan` | 1 | SIGHUP | Log reload only |

---

## Key Implementation Details by Feature

### 1. Ensuring Single Execution of Shutdown
- **Kubernetes:** `close(onlyOneSignalHandler)` panics on duplicate call
- **Kubernetes (interrupt):** `sync.Once` in Handler struct
- **Grafana:** `s.shutdownOnce sync.Once` in Server struct
- **Prometheus:** Natural through run.Group cleanup functions

### 2. Connection Draining Before Shutdown
- **Kubernetes:** Context propagation through codebase
- **Prometheus:** Explicit DrainOnShutdown flag in notifier config
- **Grafana:** `http.Server.Shutdown(ctx)` handles in-flight requests

### 3. Ordered Shutdown Dependencies
- **Kubernetes:** Context cancellation propagates automatically
- **Prometheus:** Explicit ordering in run.Group (cleanup functions called in reverse Add order)
- **Grafana:** Layered shutdown (HTTP → background services → cleanup)

### 4. Force-Exit on Second Signal
- **Kubernetes:** `os.Exit(1)` on 2nd signal received
- **Prometheus:** No explicit handling (run.Group stops naturally)
- **Grafana:** Returns from signal handler (process exits after cleanup)

### 5. Timeout Implementation
- **Kubernetes:** Implicit (context propagation)
- **Prometheus:** Per-component implementation
- **Grafana:** Explicit 30-second `context.WithTimeout`

---

### Kubernetes Additional Files
- `cmd/kube-apiserver/app/server.go` - Full apiserver startup
- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/policy/` - Admission plugin patterns
- `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/` - Leader election implementation

### Prometheus Additional Files
- `pkg/notifier/notifier.go` - Implementation of DrainOnShutdown
- `pkg/storage/` - TSDB shutdown coordination
- `cmd/prometheus/promtool/` - Command-line tool patterns

### Grafana Additional Files
- `pkg/services/` - Background service interfaces
- `pkg/modules/` - Module server implementation
- `pkg/infra/log/` - Log reload on SIGHUP implementation

# Go Graceful Shutdown Patterns - Implementation Guide

## Quick Reference

This guide provides production-ready patterns for implementing graceful shutdown in Go applications, based on analysis of three major production systems: Kubernetes, Prometheus, and Grafana.

### Executive Summary

- **Kubernetes**: Context-based cancellation with panic-on-duplicate signal handler registration
- **Prometheus**: oklog/run.Group for coordinated multi-component shutdown with explicit cleanup
- **Grafana**: Explicit timeout (30s) with sync.Once and context-based HTTP server shutdown

All three use the same core Go signal handling (`os/signal.Notify`), but differ in orchestration and cleanup patterns.

---

## Three Proven Patterns

### Pattern 1: Context-Based (Kubernetes)
**Best for:** Services with clear component hierarchy  
**Complexity:** Low  
**Dependencies:** Standard library only

```go
ctx := setupSignalContext()  // Returns cancelled context on signal
// Pass ctx to all components
<-ctx.Done()  // All components stop when ctx cancelled
```

**Advantages:**
- Automatic propagation through call stack
- Simple dependency injection
- Works with standard context.WithTimeout, context.WithDeadline

**Disadvantages:**
- Less explicit about cleanup order
- Harder to coordinate complex dependencies

### Pattern 2: Goroutine Coordination (Prometheus)
**Best for:** Complex systems with many independent services  
**Complexity:** Medium  
**Dependencies:** oklog/run (github.com/oklog/run)

```go
g := run.Group()
g.Add(execute func() error, interrupt func(error))
g.Run()  // Exits when any component returns
```

**Advantages:**
- Explicit cleanup functions for each component
- Clear dependency ordering
- All cleanups guaranteed to run

**Disadvantages:**
- Requires external library
- Steeper learning curve
- More boilerplate

### Pattern 3: Explicit Timeout (Grafana)
**Best for:** HTTP services that need bounded shutdown  
**Complexity:** Medium  
**Dependencies:** Standard library only

```go
signalChan := make(chan os.Signal, 1)
signal.Notify(signalChan, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)
<-signalChan
ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(ctx, 30*time.Second)
server.Shutdown(ctx)  // Graceful with timeout
```

**Advantages:**
- Explicit timeout prevents hanging processes
- Clear signal flow
- Good for HTTP servers

**Disadvantages:**
- Need to manage multiple signal channels
- Timeout must be chosen carefully
- Less flexible for complex scenarios

---

## Signal Configuration Quick Start

### Minimal Implementation
```go
package main

import (
    "context"
    "os"
    "os/signal"
    "syscall"
)

func setupSignalHandler() context.Context {
    ch := make(chan os.Signal, 1)
    signal.Notify(ch, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)
    
    ctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())
    go func() {
        sig := <-ch
        cancel()  // First signal stops the server
        <-ch
        os.Exit(1)  // Second signal force-exits
    }()
    
    return ctx
}

func main() {
    ctx := setupSignalHandler()
    // Use ctx for all operations
    <-ctx.Done()
    cleanup()
    os.Exit(0)
}
```

### With Timeout
```go
func handleShutdown(server *http.Server) {
    ch := make(chan os.Signal, 1)
    signal.Notify(ch, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)
    
    <-ch
    // Bounded shutdown
    ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(context.Background(), 30*time.Second)
    defer cancel()
    
    if err := server.Shutdown(ctx); err != nil {
        logger.Error("Shutdown timeout", err)
    }
}
```

### With Cleanup Functions
```go
func main() {
    handler := interrupt.New(
        func(sig os.Signal) {
            logger.Info("Shutting down", "signal", sig)
            os.Exit(0)
        },
        func() {
            logger.Info("Cleanup 1")
        },
        func() {
            logger.Info("Cleanup 2")
        },
    )
    
    err := handler.Run(func() error {
        return myServerRun()
    })
}
```

---

## Shutdown Checklist

When implementing graceful shutdown, ensure you handle:

- [ ] **Signal Registration**
  - [ ] SIGTERM (from containers, systemd)
  - [ ] SIGINT (from terminal Ctrl+C)
  - [ ] SIGHUP (for reloading, optional)
  - [ ] Second signal force-exit

- [ ] **Cleanup Order**
  - [ ] Stop accepting new connections
  - [ ] Drain in-flight requests
  - [ ] Stop background workers
  - [ ] Flush data to disk/databases
  - [ ] Close connections/listeners

- [ ] **Timeout Management**
  - [ ] Set explicit timeout (30-60 seconds recommended)
  - [ ] Handle timeout with error logging
  - [ ] Force exit if timeout exceeded

- [ ] **Coordination**
  - [ ] Prevent duplicate signal handlers
  - [ ] Ensure cleanup runs exactly once
  - [ ] Wait for all goroutines to finish
  - [ ] Log shutdown completion

- [ ] **External Integration**
  - [ ] Systemd readiness notification (optional)
  - [ ] Health check endpoint returns not-ready during shutdown
  - [ ] Load balancer can detect shutdown state

---

## Common Pitfalls and Solutions

### Pitfall 1: Lost Signals
**Problem:** Signal arrives before handler is registered  
**Solution:** Register handler early, use buffered channel with size ≥ 1

```go
// Good
ch := make(chan os.Signal, 2)  // Buffer for multiple signals
signal.Notify(ch, ...)

// Bad
ch := make(chan os.Signal)     // Unbuffered - can lose signals
```

### Pitfall 2: Infinite Wait
**Problem:** Cleanup blocks forever, process never shuts down  
**Solution:** Always use context.WithTimeout for external operations

```go
// Good
ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(ctx, 30*time.Second)
defer cancel()
server.Shutdown(ctx)

// Bad
server.Shutdown(context.Background())  // No timeout - can hang forever
```

### Pitfall 3: Duplicate Shutdown
**Problem:** Shutdown runs multiple times, corrupting state  
**Solution:** Use sync.Once for all shutdown code

```go
var shutdownOnce sync.Once

func shutdown() {
    shutdownOnce.Do(func() {
        // This code runs exactly once
    })
}
```

### Pitfall 4: Lost Cleanup
**Problem:** Some goroutines don't see cancellation  
**Solution:** Always pass context through the call chain

```go
// Good
func handleRequest(ctx context.Context) {
    select {
    case <-ctx.Done():
        return  // Stops immediately when ctx cancelled
    case <-time.After(10*time.Second):
        // Timeout
    }
}

// Bad
func handleRequest() {
    time.Sleep(10*time.Second)  // No way to interrupt
}
```

### Pitfall 5: Signal Lost on Double Handling
**Problem:** Registering signal handler twice leads to unpredictable behavior  
**Solution:** Use global sync.Once or panic on duplicate

```go
var setupOnce sync.Once

func setupSignalHandler() {
    setupOnce.Do(func() {
        ch := make(chan os.Signal, 1)
        signal.Notify(ch, ...)
        // Handler setup
    })
}
```

---

## Testing Graceful Shutdown

### Unit Test Template
```go
func TestGracefulShutdown(t *testing.T) {
    server := startServer()
    defer server.Close()
    
    // Simulate signal
    go func() {
        time.Sleep(100*time.Millisecond)
        syscall.Kill(syscall.Getpid(), syscall.SIGTERM)
    }()
    
    // Server should shut down cleanly
    ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(context.Background(), 5*time.Second)
    defer cancel()
    
    if err := server.Shutdown(ctx); err != nil {
        t.Fatalf("Shutdown failed: %v", err)
    }
}
```

### Integration Test Template
```go
func TestShutdownWithInFlightRequests(t *testing.T) {
    server := startServer()
    defer server.Close()
    
    // Start long-running request
    go makeSlowRequest(server)
    time.Sleep(100*time.Millisecond)
    
    // Trigger shutdown while request is in flight
    go func() {
        server.requestShutdown()
    }()
    
    // Wait with generous timeout
    select {
    case <-server.Done():
        // Success
    case <-time.After(5*time.Second):
        t.Fatal("Shutdown timeout")
    }
}
```

---

## Performance Considerations

### Memory Usage
- Signal channel: 1-2 signals buffered = negligible overhead
- Context overhead: Minimal (used in all modern Go code)
- sync.Once: Single byte per shutdown operation

### Latency
- Signal detection: <1ms typically (OS-dependent)
- First component stops: <10ms in well-designed systems
- Full graceful shutdown: 1-30 seconds (configurable)

### CPU Usage
- Idle signal handler: 0% CPU
- During shutdown: Brief spike during cleanup
- Worst case: One thread per waiting goroutine during timeout

### Best Practices
- Use context for free cancellation propagation
- Reserve buffer size of at least 1 for signal channels
- Set shutdown timeout to 30-60 seconds for most applications
- Log shutdown events for debugging

---

## Platform-Specific Considerations

### Linux/macOS (POSIX)
- SIGTERM: Standard container/systemd shutdown signal (use this)
- SIGINT: Keyboard interrupt (Ctrl+C)
- SIGHUP: Log rotation signal (Grafana pattern)

### Windows
- Different signals available (see os.Signal behavior)
- Consider using context directly instead of signals
- No SIGHUP equivalent

### Docker/Container
- Sends SIGTERM on stop (30-second default timeout)
- Sends SIGKILL if process doesn't exit
- Implement 15-25 second graceful shutdown

### Systemd
- Sends SIGTERM to stop service
- Respects TimeoutStopSec= in service file
- Can notify readiness with sd_notify

---

## Conclusion

Choose your pattern based on:

1. **Simple HTTP service** → Use Grafana pattern (explicit timeout)
2. **Complex multi-component system** → Use Prometheus pattern (run.Group)
3. **Microservice/controller** → Use Kubernetes pattern (context)

All three patterns are proven in production and handle the critical requirement: **graceful shutdown without losing data**.

# Graceful Shutdown in Go - Comprehensive Research Summary

## Document Overview

This document presents a detailed analysis of graceful shutdown patterns found across three production-grade Go projects:
1. **Kubernetes** - Container orchestration platform
2. **Prometheus** - Time series database and monitoring system  
3. **Grafana** - Metrics visualization and alerting platform

All code examples are extracted from official GitHub repositories and represent current best practices.

---

## Part 1: Core Concepts

### What is Graceful Shutdown?

Graceful shutdown is the process of safely terminating a running application while:
- Completing in-flight requests
- Persisting pending data
- Draining queues
- Cleaning up resources
- Notifying dependent systems

### Why It Matters

- **Data Integrity**: Prevents data loss during container restarts
- **User Experience**: Requests complete rather than timeout
- **System Health**: Proper cleanup prevents resource leaks
- **Operational Safety**: Works seamlessly with container orchestration

### Signal-Based Shutdown Flow

```
OS Signal (SIGTERM) 
    ↓
Signal Handler (os/signal.Notify)
    ↓
Context Cancellation or Channel Communication
    ↓
All Components Informed
    ↓
In-Flight Requests Drained
    ↓
Background Services Stopped
    ↓
Resources Cleaned Up
    ↓
Process Exits (0 for success, 1 for timeout/error)
```

---

## Part 2: Project Analysis

### KUBERNETES: Context-Based Cancellation

**Repository**: github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes  
**Pattern**: Propagate context.Context through all components

#### Core Files

1. **staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal.go**
   - Provides `SetupSignalContext() context.Context`
   - Returns context cancelled on SIGTERM or SIGINT
   - Guarantees single handler registration (panics if called twice)

2. **staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal_posix.go**
   - Platform-specific signal definitions
   - Handles: `os.Interrupt` (SIGINT), `syscall.SIGTERM`

3. **pkg/util/interrupt/interrupt.go**
   - Advanced handler with cleanup functions
   - Guarantees cleanup executes exactly once
   - Supports multiple signal types

#### Key Characteristics

| Aspect | Implementation |
|--------|---|
| **Signal Handling** | `signal.Notify(ch, shutdownSignals...)` |
| **Primary Signals** | SIGINT, SIGTERM |
| **Coordination** | `context.Context` propagation |
| **Cleanup Pattern** | Context cancellation |
| **Timeout** | Implicit (per-component) |
| **Double Signal** | `os.Exit(1)` on 2nd signal |
| **Dependencies** | Standard library only |

#### Code Pattern

```go
func SetupSignalContext() context.Context {
    shutdownHandler := make(chan os.Signal, 2)
    signal.Notify(shutdownHandler, shutdownSignals...)
    
    ctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())
    go func() {
        <-shutdownHandler           // 1st signal
        cancel()
        <-shutdownHandler           // 2nd signal
        os.Exit(1)
    }()
    return ctx
}

// Usage in main
ctx := SetupSignalContext()
<-ctx.Done()  // Blocks until signal
cleanup()
```

#### Advantages
- Simple, elegant design
- Automatic propagation through function calls
- Works with existing context APIs
- Minimal boilerplate

#### Use Cases
- Controllers and operators
- Microservices
- Command-line tools
- Anything with clear component hierarchy

---

### PROMETHEUS: Goroutine Orchestration

**Repository**: github.com/prometheus/prometheus  
**Pattern**: Explicit cleanup functions with oklog/run.Group

#### Core File

**cmd/prometheus/main.go** (lines 1151-1340+)
- Complex multi-component system
- 20+ goroutines managing different responsibilities
- Explicit ordering of startup and shutdown

#### Key Characteristics

| Aspect | Implementation |
|--------|---|
| **Signal Handling** | `signal.Notify(term, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)` |
| **Primary Signals** | SIGINT, SIGTERM (plus SIGHUP for reload) |
| **Coordination** | `oklog/run.Group` |
| **Cleanup Pattern** | Explicit cleanup functions per component |
| **Timeout** | Per-component (not global) |
| **Double Signal** | Natural (run.Group exits) |
| **Dependencies** | oklog/run library |

#### Code Pattern

```go
g := run.Group{}

// Signal handler
{
    term := make(chan os.Signal, 1)
    signal.Notify(term, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)
    cancel := make(chan struct{})
    
    g.Add(
        func() error {  // Execute
            <-term
            logger.Warn("Received OS signal, exiting gracefully...")
            close(cancel)
            return nil
        },
        func(error) {  // Interrupt
            webHandler.SetReady(web.Stopping)
        },
    )
}

// Each component
{
    g.Add(
        func() error { return scrapeManager.Run(...) },
        func(error) { scrapeManager.Stop() },
    )
}

g.Run()  // Blocks until any component exits
```

#### Features

1. **Multiple Signal Sources**
   - OS signal (SIGTERM/SIGINT)
   - Web API request
   - Internal cancellation

2. **Ordered Cleanup**
   - Scrape manager stops before TSDB
   - Rule manager stops (prevents false alerts)
   - Discovery managers shut down
   - Cleanup order matters critically

3. **Shutdown Flags**
   - `notifier.DrainOnShutdown` (default: true)
   - `tsdb.EnableMemorySnapshotOnShutdown`
   - `storage.remote.flush-deadline`

#### Advantages
- Explicit cleanup for each component
- Clear dependency ordering
- All cleanups guaranteed to run
- Fine-grained control

#### Use Cases
- Complex systems with many components
- Systems needing explicit ordering
- Applications with interdependent services
- Monitoring and observability systems

---

### GRAFANA: Explicit Timeout with sync.Once

**Repository**: github.com/grafana/grafana  
**Pattern**: Bounded shutdown timeout with single-execution guarantee

#### Core Files

1. **pkg/cmd/grafana-server/commands/cli.go**
   - Entry point for signal handling
   - Manages separate channels for SIGTERM/SIGINT vs SIGHUP
   - Implements 30-second shutdown timeout

2. **pkg/server/server.go**
   - Main server lifecycle management
   - `Shutdown(ctx context.Context, reason string) error`
   - Uses `sync.Once` for single execution guarantee
   - Systemd integration (NOTIFY_SOCKET)

3. **pkg/api/http_server.go**
   - HTTP listener management
   - Graceful HTTP server shutdown
   - Concurrent listener support (TCP + Unix sockets)
   - `http.ErrServerClosed` detection

#### Key Characteristics

| Aspect | Implementation |
|--------|---|
| **Signal Handling** | Separate channels for different signals |
| **Primary Signals** | SIGINT, SIGTERM (plus SIGHUP for reload) |
| **Coordination** | Context + sync.Once |
| **Cleanup Pattern** | sync.Once + context timeout |
| **Timeout** | Explicit 30 seconds |
| **Double Signal** | Returns from handler (no force-exit) |
| **Dependencies** | Standard library + sync/errgroup |

#### Code Pattern

```go
// Signal handler goroutine
func listenToSystemSignals(ctx context.Context, s gserver) {
    signalChan := make(chan os.Signal, 1)
    signal.Notify(signalChan, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)
    
    <-signalChan
    ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(ctx, 30*time.Second)
    defer cancel()
    
    if err := s.Shutdown(ctx, "System signal"); err != nil {
        fmt.Fprintf(os.Stderr, "Shutdown timeout\n")
    }
}

// Server shutdown
func (s *Server) Shutdown(ctx context.Context, reason string) error {
    var err error
    s.shutdownOnce.Do(func() {
        s.log.Info("Shutdown started", "reason", reason)
        s.managerAdapter.Shutdown(ctx, "shutdown")
        
        select {
        case <-ctx.Done():
            s.log.Warn("Timed out")
            err = fmt.Errorf("timeout")
        default:
            s.log.Debug("Shutdown complete")
        }
    })
    return err
}

// HTTP server graceful shutdown
go func() {
    <-ctx.Done()
    hs.httpSrv.Shutdown(context.Background())
}()

for _, listener := range listeners {
    errg.Go(func() error {
        err := hs.httpSrv.Serve(listener)
        if errors.Is(err, http.ErrServerClosed) {
            return nil  // Success
        }
        return err
    })
}
```

#### Special Features

1. **Multi-Signal Handling**
   ```
   SIGTERM/SIGINT → Graceful shutdown
   SIGHUP         → Log reload without shutdown
   ```

2. **Systemd Integration**
   - Notifies systemd when ready: `notifySystemd("READY=1")`
   - Reads `NOTIFY_SOCKET` environment variable
   - Communicates via Unix domain socket

3. **HTTP-Specific Optimizations**
   - Separate context for HTTP shutdown (no timeout inheritance)
   - Handles both TCP and Unix socket listeners
   - Supports HTTP, HTTP/2, HTTPS, and socket schemes

#### Advantages
- Clear timeout prevents hanging processes
- Separate signal channels for different purposes
- Well-integrated with systemd
- Explicit error handling

#### Use Cases
- HTTP/REST services
- Containerized applications
- Services managed by systemd
- Applications needing strict shutdown deadlines

---

## Part 3: Comparative Analysis

### Signal Registration

All three projects use `os/signal.Notify()` with buffered channels:

```go
// Kubernetes
shutdownHandler := make(chan os.Signal, 2)
signal.Notify(shutdownHandler, shutdownSignals...)

// Prometheus
term := make(chan os.Signal, 1)
signal.Notify(term, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)

// Grafana
signalChan := make(chan os.Signal, 1)
signal.Notify(signalChan, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)
```

**Buffer Size Selection**:
- Size 2: Kubernetes (buffer for 1st + 2nd signal)
- Size 1: Prometheus, Grafana (single signal at a time)
- General: At least 1 to avoid losing signals

### Signals Handled

| Signal | Kubernetes | Prometheus | Grafana | Purpose |
|--------|-----------|-----------|---------|---------|
| SIGINT | ✓ | ✓ | ✓ | Terminal interrupt (Ctrl+C) |
| SIGTERM | ✓ | ✓ | ✓ | Container/systemd shutdown |
| SIGHUP | ✗ | ✓ | ✓ | Reload config/logs |
| SIGQUIT | ✓ (util) | ✗ | ✗ | Quit (advanced interrupt handler) |

### Goroutine Coordination Methods

#### Kubernetes: Context Propagation
```
Signal → Context.Cancel() → All goroutines see <-ctx.Done()
```
**Propagation**: Automatic through call stack  
**Pros**: Simple, elegant  
**Cons**: Less explicit about order

#### Prometheus: run.Group
```
Signal → run.Group detects exit → Calls all interrupt functions
```
**Propagation**: Explicit via g.Add() registration  
**Pros**: Clear ordering, explicit cleanup  
**Cons**: External dependency

#### Grafana: sync.Once + Context
```
Signal → Shutdown(ctx) → sync.Once ensures single execution
```
**Propagation**: Direct method call  
**Pros**: Predictable, bounded timeout  
**Cons**: More boilerplate

### Timeout Handling

| Aspect | Kubernetes | Prometheus | Grafana |
|--------|-----------|-----------|---------|
| **Timeout Type** | Per-component | Per-component | Global (30s) |
| **Timeout Value** | Various | Various | 30 seconds |
| **Timeout Origin** | Component-specific | Component-specific | Explicit WithTimeout |
| **On Timeout** | Component-dependent | Component-dependent | Error logged, exit 1 |
| **Advantage** | Flexible | Flexible | Guaranteed exit |

### Cleanup Order Specification

#### Kubernetes
- Implicit through context propagation
- Order follows goroutine creation order
- Easy to get wrong if dependencies unclear

#### Prometheus
- Explicit in run.Group calls
- Cleanup functions called in LIFO order
- Clear and verifiable

#### Grafana
- Layered: HTTP → Services → Cleanup
- Each layer has defined timeout
- Clear separation of concerns

---

## Part 4: Implementation Patterns

### Pattern A: Minimal Context-Based (Kubernetes Style)

**When to use**: Simple applications with clear hierarchy  
**Complexity**: Low  
**Lines of code**: ~20

```go
func setupSignal() context.Context {
    ch := make(chan os.Signal, 1)
    signal.Notify(ch, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)
    ctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())
    go func() {
        <-ch
        cancel()
    }()
    return ctx
}

func main() {
    ctx := setupSignal()
    go func() {
        select {
        case <-ctx.Done():
            cleanup()
            os.Exit(0)
        }
    }()
    runServer(ctx)
}
```

### Pattern B: Goroutine-Orchestrated (Prometheus Style)

**When to use**: Complex systems with many components  
**Complexity**: Medium  
**Lines of code**: ~50-100

```go
import "github.com/oklog/run"

var g run.Group

// Signal handler
g.Add(
    func() error {
        sig := <-term
        log.Warn("Signal", "sig", sig)
        return nil
    },
    func(error) {
        log.Info("Stopping...")
    },
)

// Each component
g.Add(
    func() error { return component.Run() },
    func(error) { component.Stop() },
)

g.Run()
```

### Pattern C: Timeout-Bounded (Grafana Style)

**When to use**: HTTP services needing bounded shutdown  
**Complexity**: Medium  
**Lines of code**: ~30

```go
sig := make(chan os.Signal, 1)
signal.Notify(sig, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)

go func() {
    <-sig
    ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(
        context.Background(), 30*time.Second)
    defer cancel()
    if err := server.Shutdown(ctx); err != nil {
        log.Error("Shutdown timeout", err)
    }
}()

server.ListenAndServe()
```

---

## Part 5: Best Practices Extracted

### 1. Signal Registration

**DO:**
- Register early in main()
- Use buffered channels (size ≥ 1)
- Register exactly once (use sync.Once or panic)
- Defer to OS signal delivery until handler ready

**DON'T:**
- Call signal.Notify() multiple times without cleanup
- Use unbuffered channels
- Register late in startup sequence
- Forget to handle SIGTERM

### 2. Cleanup Ordering

**DO:**
- Stop accepting connections first
- Drain in-flight requests second
- Stop background workers third
- Flush data to storage last
- Log each step

**DON'T:**
- Stop storage before workers finish writing
- Force-close connections with pending requests
- Skip cleanup steps
- Assume goroutines see signal automatically

### 3. Timeout Management

**DO:**
- Use explicit timeouts (30-60 seconds typical)
- Context.WithTimeout for bounded operations
- Log timeout conditions
- Handle timeout as error case

**DON'T:**
- Use infinite contexts
- Expect graceful shutdown without timeout
- Ignore timeout errors
- Set timeout too short (<5 seconds)

### 4. Coordination

**DO:**
- Pass context through call stack
- Use sync.Once for shutdown code
- Log shutdown events
- Test graceful shutdown

**DON'T:**
- Create "global" shutdown flags
- Rely on goroutine panic for cleanup
- Forget to wait for goroutine completion
- Use bare select statements without default case

### 5. Error Handling

**DO:**
- Log all shutdown errors
- Distinguish timeout from cancellation
- Return error status codes appropriately
- Track shutdown completion

**DON'T:**
- Silently ignore shutdown errors
- Exit immediately on first error
- Lose error context
- Mix error types

### 6. Testing

**DO:**
- Test graceful shutdown explicitly
- Simulate signals in tests
- Verify cleanup runs
- Test timeout conditions
- Verify no data loss

**DON'T:**
- Skip shutdown testing
- Only test happy path
- Assume cleanup works
- Test with real signals in CI

---

## Part 6: Common Pitfalls and Solutions

### Pitfall 1: Lost Signals
```go
// WRONG - unbuffered channel loses signals
sig := make(chan os.Signal)
signal.Notify(sig, syscall.SIGTERM)

// CORRECT - buffered channel preserves signals
sig := make(chan os.Signal, 1)
signal.Notify(sig, syscall.SIGTERM)
```

### Pitfall 2: Infinite Waiting
```go
// WRONG - can block forever
server.Shutdown(context.Background())

// CORRECT - bounded wait
ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(context.Background(), 30*time.Second)
defer cancel()
server.Shutdown(ctx)
```

### Pitfall 3: Goroutine Leaks
```go
// WRONG - goroutine never exits
go func() {
    for {
        doWork()
    }
}()

// CORRECT - responds to context
go func() {
    for {
        select {
        case <-ctx.Done():
            return
        case <-workChan:
            doWork()
        }
    }
}()
```

### Pitfall 4: Race Conditions
```go
// WRONG - concurrent shutdown calls
s.shutdown()
s.shutdown()  // Called again

// CORRECT - synchronized with sync.Once
s.shutdownOnce.Do(func() {
    s.shutdown()
})
```

### Pitfall 5: Lost Context
```go
// WRONG - inner function ignores context
func handleRequest(ctx context.Context) {
    time.Sleep(10*time.Second)  // Can't be interrupted
}

// CORRECT - respects context
func handleRequest(ctx context.Context) {
    select {
    case <-ctx.Done():
        return
    case <-time.After(10*time.Second):
        // Process result
    }
}
```

## Part 7: File Reference Guide

### Kubernetes Files

| File | Purpose | Key Symbols |
|------|---------|---|
| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal.go` | Core signal handler | `SetupSignalContext()` |
| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal_posix.go` | POSIX signals | `shutdownSignals` |
| `pkg/util/interrupt/interrupt.go` | Advanced interrupt handler | `Handler`, `Run()` |
| `staging/src/k8s.io/sample-controller/pkg/signals/signal.go` | Template | Reference implementation |
| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/examples/leader-election/main.go` | Leader election pattern | Complete example |

### Prometheus Files

| File | Purpose | Key Symbols |
|------|---------|---|
| `cmd/prometheus/main.go` | Signal handling + orchestration | `run.Group`, signal handlers (lines 1151+) |
| `cmd/prometheus/main.go` | Feature flags | `DrainOnShutdown` (line 582) |
| `cmd/prometheus/main.go` | Memory snapshot | `EnableMemorySnapshotOnShutdown` (line 234) |

### Grafana Files

| File | Purpose | Key Symbols |
|------|---------|---|
| `pkg/cmd/grafana-server/commands/cli.go` | Signal listener | `listenToSystemSignals()` (lines 148-170) |
| `pkg/server/server.go` | Server lifecycle | `Shutdown()`, `notifySystemd()` |
| `pkg/api/http_server.go` | HTTP shutdown | `Start()`, graceful shutdown (lines 490+) |

---

## Part 8: Conclusion

All three projects implement graceful shutdown successfully using:

1. **Core Signal Handling**: `os/signal.Notify()` with buffered channels
2. **Signals**: SIGTERM and SIGINT for shutdown, SIGHUP for reload
3. **Coordination**: Context, run.Group, or sync.Once depending on complexity
4. **Cleanup**: Ordered shutdown of components, draining before stopping
5. **Timeouts**: Explicit bounds to prevent hanging processes

**Choose your pattern based on needs:**

| Requirement | Best Pattern |
|------------|---|
| Simple service with few components | **Kubernetes (context)** |
| Complex system with many services | **Prometheus (run.Group)** |
| HTTP service needing strict timeout | **Grafana (explicit timeout)** |
| Learning/reference implementation | **Kubernetes sample-controller** |

All three patterns are production-proven and handle the critical requirement: **graceful shutdown without losing data**.

### Use Context-Based Pattern (Kubernetes)

- `/tmp/kubernetes/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal.go`
- `/tmp/kubernetes/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal_posix.go`

- `SetupSignalContext() context.Context`

### Use Goroutine Coordination Pattern (Prometheus)
**When**: You have a complex system with many interdependent components  
**If**: You need explicit cleanup ordering and control

**Files**:

**Key Library**:

**Key Symbols**:
- `g.Add(execute func() error, interrupt func(error))`
- `g.Run()`

---

### Use Explicit Timeout Pattern (Grafana)
**When**: You have an HTTP service that needs bounded shutdown  
**If**: You want strict timeout and easy debugging

**Files**:
- `/tmp/grafana/pkg/cmd/grafana-server/commands/cli.go` (lines 148-170)
- `/tmp/grafana/pkg/server/server.go` (lines 155-172)
- `/tmp/grafana/pkg/api/http_server.go` (lines 490-497)

**Key Functions**:
- `listenToSystemSignals(ctx context.Context, s gserver)`

## Signal Handling Summary

### Signals to Handle

| Signal | Purpose | Kubernetes | Prometheus | Grafana |
|--------|---------|-----------|-----------|---------|
| SIGTERM | Container/systemd shutdown | ✓ | ✓ | ✓ |
| SIGINT | Terminal interrupt (Ctrl+C) | ✓ | ✓ | ✓ |
| SIGHUP | Reload config/logs | ✗ | ✓ | ✓ |

### Signal Registration

```go
// All three use buffered channels
ch := make(chan os.Signal, 1)  // or 2 for Kubernetes
signal.Notify(ch, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)
```

### On First Signal
- **Kubernetes**: Cancel context
- **Prometheus**: Log and initiate cleanup
- **Grafana**: Apply timeout, start shutdown

### On Second Signal
- **Kubernetes**: Force exit with code 1
- **Prometheus**: Natural exit from run.Group
- **Grafana**: Already exited after first signal

---

## Key Learnings

### 1. Use Buffered Channels
```go
// Buffer size 1-2 to prevent losing signals
ch := make(chan os.Signal, 1)
signal.Notify(ch, syscall.SIGTERM)
```

### 2. Always Use Timeouts
```go
// Prevent infinite waiting during shutdown
ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(ctx, 30*time.Second)
defer cancel()
server.Shutdown(ctx)
```

### 3. Ensure Single Execution
```go
// Use sync.Once for shutdown code
s.shutdownOnce.Do(func() {
    // Shutdown code runs exactly once
})
```

### 4. Explicit Cleanup Order
```go
// Stop accepting connections → drain requests → stop workers → flush data
g.Add(stopConnections, nil)
g.Add(drainRequests, nil)
g.Add(stopWorkers, nil)
g.Add(flushData, nil)
```

### 5. Pass Context Through Call Chain
```go
func handleRequest(ctx context.Context) {
    select {
    case <-ctx.Done():
        return  // Stop immediately when context cancelled
    case <-work:
        doWork()
    }
}
```

## Testing Checklist

When implementing graceful shutdown:

- [ ] Register signal handler early
- [ ] Use buffered channel (size ≥ 1)
- [ ] Handle SIGTERM and SIGINT
- [ ] Implement timeout (30-60 seconds)
- [ ] Ensure cleanup runs exactly once
- [ ] Stop connections before workers
- [ ] Log shutdown events
- [ ] Test with actual signals
- [ ] Test timeout scenario
- [ ] Verify no data loss

---

## Common Mistakes to Avoid

1. **Unbuffered signal channels** - Signals can be lost
2. **No timeout** - Process can hang indefinitely
3. **Multiple shutdown calls** - Can corrupt state
4. **Wrong cleanup order** - Workers writing to closed databases
5. **Not respecting context** - Goroutines don't see cancellation
6. **Silent errors** - Hard to debug shutdown failures

---

## Related Concepts

### Docker/Container Context
- Container sends SIGTERM on stop
- Default timeout: 30 seconds (configurable with StopTimeout)
- Then sends SIGKILL if process hasn't exited

### Systemd Context
- Sends SIGTERM on stop
- Respects `TimeoutStopSec=` in service file
- Can use `Type=notify` with `sd_notify()` for readiness
- Grafana implements `notifySystemd("READY=1")`

### Kubernetes Context
- Graceful termination period: 30 seconds (configurable)
- POD lifecycle hooks available (PreStop)
- Health check endpoints should return not-ready during shutdown

## The Three Patterns at a Glance

### Pattern 1: Context-Based (Kubernetes)
**File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal.go`

```go
ctx := SetupSignalContext()  // Returns context cancelled on signal
<-ctx.Done()                 // Blocks until signal
cleanup()                    // All components already stopped
```

**Best for**: Simple services, clear component hierarchy  
**Complexity**: Low  
**Dependencies**: Standard library only

---

### Pattern 2: Goroutine Coordination (Prometheus)
**File**: `cmd/prometheus/main.go` (lines 1151+)

```go
g := run.Group{}
g.Add(executeFunc, cleanupFunc)  // For each component
g.Add(executeFunc, cleanupFunc)
g.Run()  // Exits when any component returns
```

**Best for**: Complex systems, many interdependent services  
**Complexity**: Medium  
**Dependencies**: github.com/oklog/run

---

### Pattern 3: Explicit Timeout (Grafana)
**Files**: `pkg/cmd/grafana-server/commands/cli.go`, `pkg/server/server.go`

```go
<-signalChan
ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(ctx, 30*time.Second)
defer cancel()
server.Shutdown(ctx)  // Bounded graceful shutdown
```

**Best for**: HTTP services, containerized apps  
**Complexity**: Medium  
**Dependencies**: Standard library + sync/errgroup

## Key Facts About Each Project

### Kubernetes (github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes)
- **Pattern**: Context-based cancellation
- **Key File**: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal.go`
- **Signals**: SIGINT, SIGTERM
- **Approach**: Return context from signal handler, propagate through codebase
- **Timeout**: Implicit (per-component)
- **Force-Exit**: Yes (os.Exit(1) on 2nd signal)

### Prometheus (github.com/prometheus/prometheus)
- **Pattern**: Goroutine coordination with oklog/run.Group
- **Key File**: `cmd/prometheus/main.go` (lines 1151-1340+)
- **Signals**: SIGINT, SIGTERM, SIGHUP
- **Approach**: Explicit cleanup functions per component
- **Timeout**: Per-component implementation
- **Force-Exit**: Natural (run.Group handles it)

### Grafana (github.com/grafana/grafana)
- **Pattern**: Explicit timeout with sync.Once
- **Key Files**: 
  - `pkg/cmd/grafana-server/commands/cli.go` (signal handler)
  - `pkg/server/server.go` (shutdown logic)
  - `pkg/api/http_server.go` (HTTP graceful shutdown)
- **Signals**: SIGINT, SIGTERM, SIGHUP (separate handling)
- **Approach**: Bounded shutdown with 30-second timeout
- **Timeout**: Explicit global timeout
- **Force-Exit**: No (returns from signal handler)

## Signal Handling Summary

All three projects handle these signals:

| Signal | Meaning | Handling |
|--------|---------|----------|
| SIGTERM | Shutdown from container/systemd | Graceful shutdown |
| SIGINT | Ctrl+C from terminal | Graceful shutdown |
| SIGHUP | Config/log reload | Reload without shutdown |

All use `os/signal.Notify()` with buffered channels (size 1-2).

## Critical Implementation Points

### 1. Use Buffered Channels
```go
ch := make(chan os.Signal, 1)  // Don't use unbuffered
signal.Notify(ch, syscall.SIGTERM, os.Interrupt)
```

### 2. Always Use Timeout
```go
ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(ctx, 30*time.Second)
defer cancel()
server.Shutdown(ctx)  // Won't hang forever
```

### 3. Ensure Single Execution
```go
s.shutdownOnce.Do(func() {
    // This code runs exactly once
})
```

### 4. Log Everything
```go
logger.Info("Shutdown started", "reason", reason)
logger.Warn("Timed out waiting for shutdown")
logger.Info("Shutdown complete")
```

### 5. Pass Context Through Call Stack
```go
func handler(ctx context.Context) {
    select {
    case <-ctx.Done():
        return  // Responds to cancellation
    case <-workChan:
        doWork()
    }
}
```

                         SIGNAL HANDLING SUMMARY
================================================================================

All three projects use: os/signal.Notify() with buffered channels

Signals Handled:
  SIGTERM    - Container/systemd shutdown signal (primary)
  SIGINT     - Terminal interrupt (Ctrl+C)
  SIGHUP     - Config/log reload (Prometheus & Grafana)

Buffer Sizes:
  Kubernetes: 2 (for 1st + 2nd signal)
  Prometheus: 1
  Grafana:    1 per signal type

  ch := make(chan os.Signal, 1)
  signal.Notify(ch, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)

================================================================================
                        KEY IMPLEMENTATION POINTS
================================================================================

1. USE BUFFERED CHANNELS
   ✓ ch := make(chan os.Signal, 1)
   ✗ ch := make(chan os.Signal)

2. ALWAYS USE TIMEOUT
   ✓ ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(ctx, 30*time.Second)
   ✗ server.Shutdown(context.Background())

3. ENSURE SINGLE EXECUTION
   ✓ s.shutdownOnce.Do(func() { cleanup() })
   ✗ Multiple shutdown() calls possible

4. EXPLICIT CLEANUP ORDER
   Kubernetes: Implicit through context propagation
   Prometheus: Explicit in run.Group order
   Grafana: Layered (HTTP → Services → Cleanup)

5. PASS CONTEXT THROUGH CALL STACK
   ✓ func handler(ctx context.Context) { <-ctx.Done() }
   ✗ func handler() { time.Sleep(...) } // Can't interrupt

6. LOG SHUTDOWN EVENTS
   - Shutdown started (with reason)
   - Timeout warnings
   - Shutdown completion
   - Error conditions

================================================================================
                         GRACEFUL SHUTDOWN FLOW
================================================================================

All three projects follow this general flow:

OS Signal (SIGTERM)
    ↓
Signal Handler (os/signal.Notify)
    ↓
Context Cancellation or Channel Communication
    ↓
All Components Informed
    ↓
Stop Accepting New Requests
    ↓
Drain In-Flight Requests (with timeout)
    ↓
Stop Background Goroutines
    ↓
Flush Data to Storage
    ↓
Close Resources
    ↓
Process Exits (0 for success, 1 for timeout)

Timeout typically: 30-60 seconds

MINIMAL CONTEXT-BASED (Copy-Paste Ready)
----------------------------------------
func setupSignalHandler() context.Context {
    ch := make(chan os.Signal, 1)
    signal.Notify(ch, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)
    ctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())
    go func() {
        <-ch
        cancel()       // First signal
        <-ch
        os.Exit(1)     // Second signal
    }()
    return ctx
}

WITH TIMEOUT (Copy-Paste Ready)
------------------------------
ch := make(chan os.Signal, 1)
signal.Notify(ch, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)

go func() {
    <-ch
    ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(context.Background(), 30*time.Second)
    defer cancel()
    if err := server.Shutdown(ctx); err != nil {
        logger.Error("Shutdown timeout", err)
    }
}()

WITH CLEANUP FUNCTIONS (Copy-Paste Ready)
-----------------------------------------
handler := interrupt.New(
    func(sig os.Signal) {
        logger.Info("Shutting down", "signal", sig)
        os.Exit(0)
    },
    func() { logger.Info("Cleanup 1") },
    func() { logger.Info("Cleanup 2") },
)

err := handler.Run(func() error {
    return myServerRun()
})

================================================================================
                         COMMON PITFALLS
================================================================================

PITFALL 1: Lost Signals
Problem: Signal arrives before handler registered
Solution: Use buffered channel (size ≥ 1)

PITFALL 2: Infinite Wait
Problem: Cleanup blocks forever, process never exits
Solution: Always use context.WithTimeout for external operations

PITFALL 3: Duplicate Shutdown
Problem: Shutdown runs multiple times, corrupts state
Solution: Use sync.Once for all shutdown code

PITFALL 4: Lost Cleanup
Problem: Some goroutines don't see cancellation
Solution: Always pass context through call chain

PITFALL 5: Wrong Cleanup Order
Problem: Workers writing to closed database
Solution: Stop accepting → drain → stop workers → flush → close
